Three new U.S.-centric pillars established between 2022 and 2025 form the framework of this section: (1) Platform Technology Designation (FDCA §506K), (2) Advanced Manufacturing Technologies (AMT, FD&C §506L), and (3) Distributed Manufacturing (DM)/point-of-care (POC) Manufacturing Framework (21 CFR). 211.110·FRAME). Here, PreCheck (2025), an onshoring pilot, and international counterparts (MHRA, EMA, EU) are attached as adjacent mechanisms.

The output of this section flows in two directions. One is to lighten the 8.1 submission by referring to and utilizing prior data as “prior knowledge” in subsequent applications through designation, and the other is to connect with the 8.2 inspection through the facility preparation stage (PreCheck) and distributed quality supervision (DM/POC). Let’s nail down an important premise first — neither designation lowers quality standards. Designation only provides efficiency and predictability in screening, but does not replace the burden of proving safety, purity, and potency.

How It Works (1) — Platform Technology Designation (§506K)

The Platform Technology Designation Program was created by the FDA to fulfill the requirements of FDCA §506K(b), which was passed as part of the “PREVENT Pandemics Act” in December 2022, and provides a path to accelerate the review of drugs and biologics that use platform technologies (Source). Here, “platform technology” is defined as a well-understood and reproducible technology such as nucleic acid sequence, molecular structure, mechanism of action, delivery means, vector, or a combination thereof (Source). It soon becomes clear why this definition emerged from pandemic response legislation — mRNA vaccines, which simply replace the sequence of the same LNP carrier, fit exactly into this picture.

To receive the designation, three statutory requirements must be met: The first is a prior approval requirement, in which the platform technology must already be included in or used in an FDA-approved product. Second, it has multi-product potential, which means it must have the potential to be used for more than one drug without adverse effects on quality, manufacturing, and safety. Third is process efficiency, which requires a reasonable probability of bringing significant efficiency to the development, manufacturing, and screening process (Source). Here, the key criterion for the second requirement is “minimal differences.” There should be minimal differences between the approved or licensed drug using the platform and the investigational drug, and these differences can be supported by evidence such as similarity in structure, mechanism of action, formulation, and manufacturing process (Source).

Application timing and processing procedures are also standardized. The FDA recommends that you request designation at the IND stage for a planned NDA/BLA and will decide whether to grant designation within 90 days of receiving your request (Source). The compensation is to allow the platform itself to be referenced and utilized as prior knowledge rather than being reexamined for each subsequent product. However, if the requirements are no longer met, the designation may be withdrawn.

How it works (2) — AMT designation (§506L)

The second pillar, the AMT designation program, derives from §3213 of the Food and Drug Omnibus Reform Act (FDORA) of 2022 (21 U.S.C. §356l), which requires the target technology to substantially improve the manufacturing process while maintaining equal or superior quality (Source). Examples of target technologies include continuous manufacturing, 3D printing of finished pharmaceutical products, modular manufacturing platforms, and advanced process analysis technology (PAT), and the final guidance for December 2024 confirms the draft of the same name published on December 13, 2023 (Source). Because of this list, AMT is directly connected to node 5.4, which deals with continuous and intensified processes and PAT and digitalization — if that is the “substance of the technology,” then 8.3 is responsible for “regulatory recognition and compensation for that technology.”

What makes AMT crucially different from other FDA-mandated programs is that it is independent of the submission of a specific application. AMT designation may be used to support the development of a specific investigational drug or a new formulation of an approved drug, but may also be granted to the technology itself, unrelated to any specific application (Source). Thanks to the nature of this “designation given to technology,” even contract manufacturers (CDMOs) or equipment and technology developers that do not have a specific product can receive the designation. In fact, sponsors, contract manufacturers, and technology developers can request designation, and FDA recommends early communication with CDER’s Emerging Technology Team (ETT) or CBER’s Advanced Technologies Team (Source).

There are three types of compensation that designated holders receive. The FDA accelerates the development and review of applications using designated technologies, allows reference and use of data and information about the technology in subsequent applications, and provides timely advice and additional communication. At the same time, FDA does not intend for a designated AMT to increase the time it takes to evaluate or the number of evaluation cycles (Source). There is one validity condition: the AMT designation program has a sunset date of October 1, 2032 ⚠️(Source).

How It Works (3) — Distributed/Onsite (DM/POC) Manufacturing and 21 CFR 211.110

The third axis is the trend of changing the physical architecture of manufacturing itself. Distributed manufacturing (DM) is a distributed strategy that places manufacturing units in multiple locations, and on-site (POC) manufacturing is a subset of it, in which manufacturing units are placed at host sites close to patient treatment locations, such as medical institutions (Source). Modalities that benefit from being “made at the patient’s side,” such as autologous CAR-T, are a natural source of demand for this architecture. The origins of this regulatory effort are the Framework for Regulatory Advanced Manufacturing Evaluation (FRAME) initiative, launched in 2021, which seeks to examine legal authorities and regulations to support advanced manufacturing technologies ⚠️(Source).The regulatory key is how to apply the existing CGMP, especially 21 CFR 211.110 (batch uniformity and in-process management), which was used on the premise of a centralized batch plant, to distributed and automated units. In response, the draft guidance “Considerations for Complying with 21 CFR 211.110” announced by the FDA in January 2025 applies to human and veterinary drugs (including biotechnology products, excluding raw drug products), and covers cases where advanced manufacturing (e.g. 3D printing/continuous manufacturing) and process models are used as part of a commercial control strategy. Deals with it (Source). A key requirement of this guidance is that process models are recognized but not left to stand alone — to ensure compliance with 211.110, process models must be coupled with in-process material testing or process monitoring (Source). The oversite model is a structure in which a central quality organization manages distributed sites, and aims to prevent multiple POC sites from requiring separate permits from the central site’s manufacturing permit.

PreCheck is also worth mentioning as an adjacent mechanism. The FDA PreCheck program is intended to increase the regulatory predictability of domestic manufacturing in response to Executive Order 14293 (“Regulation Relaxation for Domestic Production of Core Drugs”) and is operated in two stages: the facility preparation stage (a stage of comprehensive submission of facility-specific information using Type V DMF and more frequent communication with the FDA) and the application submission stage ⚠️ (Source). This facility preparation stage becomes the point of contact that accelerates the inspection (8.2).

Key parameters/materials — The materials in this section are not reagents, but laws, designations, and frameworks.

The “materials” covered in 8.3 are regulatory tools, not media or reagents. At the level of laws and regulations, FDCA §506K (platform designation), FD&C §506L=21 U.S.C. §356l (AMT), its parent body, FDORA 2022, 21 CFR 211.110 (batch uniformity and in-process management), 21 CFR 314.54 (path to utilize existing data), which has overlapping platform designation and functions, and Executive Order 14293, which is the basis for onshoring. A summary of each mechanism at the program mechanism level is as follows — the platform has a parameter set of three statutory requirements, IND phase application, 90-day decision, and data reference (Source); AMT is independent of specific applications, recommends early communication of ETT/CATT, and has a sunset in 2032 (Source); DM/POC is characterized by a proximity host site, central oversite, and single manufacturing license orientation (Source).

Specific examples of technologies eligible for designation include continuous manufacturing, 3D printing, modular manufacturing platforms, advanced PAT, and automated cell therapy platforms (Source). Current figures are still crude. In AMT, Cellares became the first company to receive designation from CBER for its automated cell therapy manufacturing platform “Cell Shuttle” in early April 2025 (Source). On the other hand, as of October 16, 2025, CDER received 5 designation requests from 5 organizations after the enforcement of §506L, but 0 were designated and 3 were under review ⚠️(Source). As an international counterpart, the MHRA launched a decentralized/on-site (POC) manufacturing framework in June 2025 to enable close-quarter manufacturing of personalized treatments and ensure that multiple POC manufacturing sites do not require a separate license from the manufacturing license granted to the central site ⚠️ (Source).

What is judged from a quality and regulatory perspective?

Rather than performing a test, this section determines “whether innovative manufacturing and platform reuse can be accepted without compromising quality.” The judgment target varies depending on the mechanism. In the platform, evidence supporting the “minimal difference” between the approved product and the test drug (similarity in structure, mechanism of action, formulation, and manufacturing process) and no impact on quality are the criteria for judgment (Source). In the AMT, the criteria are whether the manufacturing process can be substantially improved while maintaining equal or superior quality (Source), and in DM/POC, the criteria for determining overall distribution unit Batch uniformity, in-process management, and equivalence between sites are subject to judgment (Source).Several key regulatory principles run through this decision. Platform technology is eligible for designation only when it is used in an already approved product and a minimum difference is proven, and is withdrawn if the requirements are not met (Source). AMT is designed so that the technology can be granted independently of the specific application, while not increasing the review cycle (Source). DM/POC is also subject to full CGMP, and the process model must be combined with in-process testing (Source). The way these designations are linked to 8.1 (submission) and 8.2 (inspection) is also an extension of this principle — the data secured through designation lightens subsequent submissions, PreCheck’s facility preparation stage accelerates inspection, and DM/POC changes the inspection model premised on a centralized batch plant to a distributed oversite.

Here, a quality issue unique to product modality stands out. Gene therapy stakeholders point out that the safety risk of the platform comes from the inserted gene sequence/payload rather than the delivery vehicle (capsid/LNP), and even if the same capsid has a different promoter or payload, the expression results in the tissue are believed to be greatly different ⚠️(Source). In other words, the logic that “the means of delivery are the same, so a relaxed review is applied” is directly subject to debate from a quality and safety perspective.

Differences in effectiveness by product type

Although these new mechanisms nominally apply across modalities, their actual value varies greatly by product type. For mAbs and recombinant proteins, platform technology designation is the most natural fit — because the “platform process” for mAbs is already mature and it is easy to make a minimal difference argument. AMT is applied to continuous/reinforcement processes and PAT to replace or complement large stainless steel batch plants, and POC/DM demand is low in this product modality.

mRNA-LNP is a strong candidate for platform designation because it is structured to replace only the sequence of the same LNP carrier. It is also directly related to the fact that §506K was newly created with the motive of rapid response to the pandemic (Source), and it is at this point that the debate surrounding “minimum difference” and “sequence-derived safety” becomes most acute.

Viral vectors/CGT (AAV/Lenti/CAR-T) are the most subtle cases. Although the platform designation was intended to help AAV capsid and lenti platforms, stakeholders believe that a frame based on small molecules does not fit well with CGT. Current requirements developed for small molecules do not adequately address the unique needs of CGT manufacturing, because process improvements for CGTs occur throughout the life of product development, including post-marketing — in many CGT development programs, after early clinical benefits have been identified, process changes to scale up manufacturing are made only at later stages ⚠️ (Source). Conversely, AMT is very related to CGT — as we saw earlier, the Cellares “Cell Shuttle” was the first to receive AMT designation (Source), and POC/DM has the greatest potential for near-patient manufacturing of autologous CAR-T. In summary, these mechanisms are nominally regardless of product modality, but their effective values ​​differ greatly in new modalities (especially CGT·mRNA), and the frame suitability debate is the greatest in that product modality.

Practices and recent changes

The current standard states that these mechanisms are “optional new tracks on top of the standard path” and are still in their early stages and adoption is low. Looking at the movement over the past three years chronologically, FDORA 2022 simultaneously created both platform (§506K) and AMT (§506L) designations (Source), which were then specified as guidance for 2024-2025 — the final AMT guidance was drafted in December 2023. (Source), and the 211.110 compliance draft was released in January 2025 (Source). Although the first AMT designation was granted to CGT automation equipment (Cellares Cell Shuttle, CBER, April 2025) (Source), CDER adoption is very minimal, with 5 cases received and 0 designations as of October 2025 ⚠️(Source). In addition, the creation of PreCheck added to the trend of strengthening onshoring and facility predictability ⚠️(Source), and internationally, the MHRA POC framework (June 2025) moved to support distributed and advanced manufacturing ⚠️(Source).Contact points with adjacent nodes also become clear in this flow. AMT explicitly compensates for continuous manufacturing, PAT, modular, 3D printing, and automation, so it is directly connected to node 5.4, which deals with continuous/enhanced processes and digitalization (Source), and POC/DM overturns centralized manufacturing and is aligned with close manufacturing of CGT/mRNA (Part 9) (Source). Limitations are also evident — low adoption rates and questionable added value, inadequate CGT frame of reference for small molecules, the “same delivery ≠ same safety” safety argument, regulatory uncertainty and harmonization gaps among countries in DM/POC, and timing uncertainty from the sunset clause (2032) and multiple draft stages.

Issue: Three points of difference in judgment

Issue 1 - Does designation really provide real benefits?The argument for designation is that it accelerates development and review and increases regulatory predictability by allowing platforms and technologies to be referenced and utilized as prior knowledge rather than being reexamined for each subsequent product (90-day decision, AMT independent of application, data reference). The other side believes that adoption is very low (5 cases received and 0 cases designated as of CDER AMT in October 2025) and effectiveness is uncertain. In fact, some stakeholders are questioning whether platform designation has any clear benefits compared to existing data utilization pathways under 21 CFR §314.54, and one regulator even expressed that this program “may be more of a PR stunt than anything else” ⚠️(Source). Judgments of “formal introduction” and “practical use” are divided in the gap between the design advantages of the new designated program and the overlap with existing pathways and initial low adoption.Issue 2 — Is platform reuse based on the same delivery method safe in CGT? The design intent of §506K is to view the same vector/delivery platform as a well-understood, reproducible technology and justify efficient development and review with the minimum difference argument. However, the opposing view points out that the safety risk comes from the inserted gene sequence and payload, not the delivery method, and that even for the same capsid, if the promoter and payload are different, the expression varies greatly, so “same delivery method → ​​mitigation screening” may overlook the risk ⚠️(Source). This is where the premise of the regulatory frame (delivery vehicle dominates risk) and the reality of CGT biology (sequence/payload dominate risk/efficacy) clash.Issue 3 - Is the existing CGMP (211.110) appropriately applied to distributed manufacturing? The FDA believes that 211.110 can also be applied to distributed units through in-process management and process models (in parallel with testing) with a science- and risk-based frame, and proposes a model that governs multiple sites with a central oversite and single manufacturing license (Source). On the other hand, there is a counterargument that 211.110 was initially used on the premise of a centralized batch plant, so batch uniformity and physical separation of samples during processing are difficult in distributed and continuous units, and there is a large gap and uncertainty in regulatory harmonization between countries in DM technology. Because of the structural gap between “central batch manufacturing” assumed by CGMP and actual “distributed, automated, and continuous proximity manufacturing,” the judgments of regulators and industry are divided.Unresolved questions: (1) The original texts (PDF) of the four FDA guidances were binary, so direct verbatim quotations could not be obtained, so the definitions, requirements, and compensation phrases were obtained from law firm client alert·RAPS·Federal Register summary and the FDA program page, and comparison of the original text was not performed. (2) Whether the platform technology designation guidance will be finalized as of 2026 (whether the final version will take effect after draft 2024-05) and the actual number and cases of designation are not yet confirmed — AMT has secured the final version and figures, but the platform has only been secured based on the draft stage. (3) Mapping of the text of the separate CGMP guidance for DM/POC (announced “Approaches to Meeting CGMP Requirements for Distributed Manufacturing”) and specific regulations for single manufacturing license/site registration, and harmonization details between EU/US secured only at an overview level (overlapping with nodes 8.2 and 9.2). (4) International (MHRA POC, EMA ATMP GMP Part IV, EU pharmaceutical law revision) details were secured only at the consulting blog/summary level - Verbatim comparison of the original guidelines was not performed.

9. Modality-specific process architectures

Where the general (protein/mAb-shaped) spine bends: modalities whose process flow inverts or replaces core unit operations.

9.1 mRNA/LNP manufacturing

The role of this clause — the point where the entire spine is ‘replaced’

In Part 9, which deals with process architecture by product type, mRNA/LNP manufacturing is where the framework of the protein/antibody (mAb) process changes most dramatically. A key feature is that this process is a ‘cell-free’ reaction that does not use any cells, and this property allows for short production lead times and relatively simple manufacturing (Source). Cell culture and fermentation (Part 2), which supported the upstream process in traditional biopharmaceuticals, and Protein A affinity capture (Node 3.1), which held the target protein downstream, disappear here, and in-vitro transcription (IVT) and oligo-dT/ion pair purification are replaced. As a result, unlike in mAb, where the cell line is the starting material, in mRNA, the template DNA coming from node 1.3 actually becomes the starting material, strengthening the nature of a platform where only the sequence needs to be changed. This section takes as input the linearized DNA template in node 1.3 and the LNP formulation strategy in node 4.1 and (i) creates an mRNA drug substance (Drug Substance) by IVT, (ii) forms a drug product (drug product) by encapsulating the mRNA in ionized lipid nanoparticles (LNP), and then (iii) performs sterile filtration and filling (node 4.2) and ultra-low temperature cold chain (node 4.2). Skip to 4.4).

How the process works — from mold to encapsulation

The end-to-end flow follows the sequence [mold preparation → IVT → mRNA purification → LNP encapsulation → post-processing]. Specifically, circular pDNA is linearized, an IVT capable of selecting co-transcriptional capping is run, and after the desired incubation time, DNase-I is added to the reaction solution to decompose the DNA template, followed by purification by chromatography, lipids are mixed to form LNPs, and then charged through dialysis and sterile filtration ([Source] (https://www.advancingrna.com/doc/end-to-end-mrna-ds-and-dp-manufacturing-processes-0001)).The mRNA produced in the first step, IVT, is controlled by five structural elements: 5’ cap, 5’ untranslated region (UTR), coding region (ORF), 3’ UTR, and poly-adenosine (A) tail (Source). Among these, the method of attaching the 5’ cap (capping) is a critical step that determines how mRNA is recognized within the cell. While cells treat mRNA in the form of Cap 0 as foreign RNA and activate the innate immune response upon introduction, Cap 1, which adds 2’-O methylation to the nucleotide following m7G, avoids this innate immune recognition, lowering the possibility of an immune response when administered in-vivo (Source). ⚠️

There are two competing routes to actually attach the cap. (a) Co-transcriptional capping is a method of forming Cap 1 in one reaction by adding a trinucleotide cap analog (e.g. CleanCap) to the IVT reaction, and (b) enzymatic capping is a method of adding vaccinia/faustovirus capping enzyme in a separate step after IVT is completed. CleanCap, an idle-transfer method, produces a capping efficiency exceeding 95%, while ARCA, another idle-transfer analogue, is reported to have an efficiency as low as 50-80% (Source). ⚠️ Meanwhile, conversion of approximately 100% of the 5’-triphosphate transcript to capped mRNA is typically achievable with enzyme-based capping (Source). ⚠️ Which route to take depends on the scale, with co-transcriptional capping being recommended for most bench-scale applications, while enzymatic capping is presented as the recommended approach for large-scale or mRNA manufacturing (Source). ⚠️ (See ‘Issues’ below for this standardization debate.)

After IVT, we move on to tablets. The core of this step is oligo-dT affinity chromatography using the poly(A) tail, which uses the principle of selective binding of short dT oligos to the poly(A) tail of mRNA to achieve purity exceeding 99% in all elution fractions, with no NTP impurities detected (Source). However, there remains a problem that does not go away even with tablets. Product-related impurities such as immunogenic double-stranded RNA (dsRNA), abortive transcripts, truncated RNA, and RNA-DNA hybrids remain a challenge, and dsRNA removal is especially important in mRNA therapeutic applications (Source). The root of the problem is physical similarity. The dsRNA by-product is similar in size to the original single-stranded transcript and, in the case of a 3’ hairpin extension, even has a poly-A tail, so it cannot be removed by size exclusion chromatography (SEC), tangential flow filtration (TFF), or poly-dT affinity chromatography (Source). Therefore, a separate orthogonal process such as the cellulose method or ion pair reversed phase (IP-RP) is additionally required.

The purified mRNA is now encapsulated in LNPs. LNPs are usually composed of four main components: ionized lipids that bind to negatively charged biomaterials and help endosome escape, phospholipids that provide structure, cholesterol that contributes to stability and membrane fusion, and PEG-lipids that improve stability and circulation (Source). ⚠️ When these four lipids are rapidly mixed with the organic phase dissolved in ethanol and the mRNA contained in the low pH (~4) water phase, the protonated ionized lipids electrostatically bind to the negatively charged mRNA, and as the ethanol is momentarily diluted, the lipids self-assemble and precipitate into nanoparticles. The physics governing particle quality is interesting here. The quality properties (particle size, PDI, encapsulation efficiency, and morphology) of LNPs are determined as a result of competition between the ‘time scale of nucleic acid-lipid interaction’ and the ‘time scale of lipid self-assembly’, and rapid mixing compresses these two time scales, causing all lipid molecules to simultaneously undergo the transition from the organic solvent to the aqueous phase, creating uniformly sized particles (Source). In practice, the microfluidic system reaches a critical ethanol concentration (60-80%) within milliseconds, ensuring homogeneous nucleation, and obtains LNPs with a diameter of approximately 100 nm and an encapsulation efficiency exceeding 80% at a flow rate ratio (FRR) of 3:1 (Source). ⚠️

In the final post-processing, the organic solvent is removed and the buffer solution is changed. TFF stabilizes LNP by removing more than 95% of ethanol within 4 minutes and exchanging the buffer by diafiltration (Source). ⚠️ The formation buffer (low pH) is exchanged and concentrated with the storage buffer (neutral ~7.4), then aseptically filtered and filled, and optionally freeze-dried.

Key parameters and materials

Among the control factors for IVT reaction, the Mg2+ concentration is considered to be the most influential process variable (CPP). In a self-amplifying RNA (saRNA) optimization study, Mg2+ was found to be the CPP with the greatest impact on yield (Source). In fact, when IVT of 8.5 kb saRNA was performed under the conditions of 60 ng/µL of DNA template, Mg2+ 52 mM, 2 hours, and 10 mM of cap analog, 5 U/µL of T7 RNAP, 86.5% integrity was obtained with an expected yield of 1121.5 µg, and the difference in neutralizing antibody titer between 80% and 37% integrity was 137-fold, indicating that integrity is simple. It shows that it is not a quality indicator but is directly related to efficacy (Source).The purity and yield indicators of the purified product are confirmed in the previous oligo-dT chromatography performance (purity exceeding 99%) ([Source] (https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC11458983/)), and representative values for LNP include critical ethanol of 60-80% in microfluidic mixing, FRR 3:1, target particle size of approximately 100 nm, and encapsulation efficiency of over 80%. (Source). ⚠️ Encapsulation efficiency is usually managed at 90-98% in vaccine products (Source). The poly(A) tail affects the stability and translation efficiency of mRNA and is usually designed to be 100 to 150 nt long, and both length and heterogeneity are evaluated (Source). A particularly important constraint in terms of raw materials is supply qualifications. IVT process components, especially enzymes used in the capping step, must be sourced from certified suppliers who ensure that all materials are animal-free and GMP-grade (Source).

Quality attributes and regulations

mRNA-DS and LNP-DP each have their own set of key quality attributes (CQAs). On the mRNA side, capping efficiency is defined as a percentage of the sum of the total 5’ capped mRNA and process-related 5’ species in the sample, and mRNA integrity, 5’ capping, and poly(A) are analyzed together by IP-RP HPLC (Source). The most important encapsulation efficiency on the LNP side is calculated by dividing the encapsulated mRNA by subtracting the free mRNA from the total mRNA by the total mRNA (Source). The analysis method also has pitfalls. The RiboGreen fluorescent dye method is the current standard and USP recommended test for measuring mRNA-LNP encapsulation efficiency, but it does not distinguish between full-length mRNA and degraded species (Source). Therefore, orthogonal analysis such as CGE-LIF is used to simultaneously view integrity. In addition, to analyze LNP encapsulated samples, existing test methods could not be used as is, so the methods for DNA content, dsRNA, bioburden, and endotoxin tests had to be adapted for encapsulated samples (Source).

The regulatory framework has been rapidly being overhauled recently. EMA released the draft guidelines for quality aspects of mRNA vaccines in March 2025 (comment deadline 2025-09-30), defining starting materials as nucleotides, 5’ cap/capping reagents, and linear DNA templates, and defining raw materials as mRNA and requiring CQAs to be derived from QTPP (target product quality characteristics) (Source). In the European Pharmacopoeia (Ph.Eur.), three new texts will be introduced in July 2025 covering mRNA-LNP vaccines for human use, mRNA raw materials for vaccine production, and linear DNA templates used as starting materials (Source). However, regulatory gaps clearly remain. There is still no international consensus on whether mRNA-LNP vaccine components should be viewed as starting materials or excipients (Source).

Modality Variation — This clause itself is an ‘inversion’

This section is the point of Spine’s reversal, and the description of variation also begins with contrast with other modalities. As summarized earlier, compared to mAb, upstream cell culture and downstream Protein A capture are completely eliminated, cell-free IVT and oligo-dT purification take their place, and the starting material is changed to template DNA rather than cell line (Source). The most prominent of the downstream mutations is self-amplifying RNA (saRNA). The length of saRNA is 8.5 to 11.5 kb because it contains a replicase sequence, and the key challenge is that this extended length causes premature termination during IVT and reduces product integrity (Source). Nonetheless, the process itself is shared. saRNA and conventional mRNA share the same production workflow of plasmid production, linearization, IVT, mRNA purification, and LNP encapsulation, but saRNA requires additional optimization specific to integrity as well as yield (Source).

Practices and recent changes

The current standard process is batch IVT → DNase treatment → oligo-dT/IP-RP purification → microfluidic or impinging-jet rapid mixing LNP → TFF buffer exchange → aseptic filling. The remaining limitations largely fall into two axes. The first is the dsRNA removal challenge seen earlier (Source), and the second is the scale-up nonlinearity of the mixer. The rapid and turbulent mixing achieved in microfluidic chips is difficult to reproduce in larger pipes or containers, resulting in less efficient and less uniform mixing, resulting in larger, more dispersed particles and lower encapsulation efficiency (Source). ⚠️ So, industries use different mixers depending on their size. The confined impinging jet mixer (IJM), which directly collides two high-velocity countercurrents, has become the method of choice for large-scale mRNA vaccine production during the COVID pandemic, but its large minimum working volume makes it unsuitable for initial screening, and conversely, the staggered herringbone micromixer has a throughput of less than 100 mL/h, making it a bottleneck for GMP scale implementation (Source).The direction of movement in recent years can be summarized as continuity and concentration, regulatory overhaul, and clinical entry of new RNA modalities. Continuous (multi-column) oligo-dT chromatography is estimated to increase productivity by 5.75 times and reduce operating costs by 15% compared to batches, while maintaining yields exceeding 90%, mRNA integrity exceeding 95%, and purity exceeding 99%, providing evidence that continuous purification process provides substantial benefits (Source). In terms of new modalities, saRNA has moved beyond clinical trials and entered the commercial stage. ARCT-154, a self-amplifying RNA COVID-19 vaccine jointly developed by CSL and Arcturus Therapeutics, was approved by Japan’s Ministry of Health, Labor and Welfare on November 27, 2023, becoming the world’s first commercially approved saRNA vaccine (Source). ⚠️

Issue:There are three points in this section where a single standard has not yet been established. First, it is a capping method for large-scale GMP manufacturing. NEB recommends enzymatic capping for large-scale/mRNA manufacturing, citing approximately 100% conversion as the basis (Source) ⚠️. Conversely, co-transfer CleanCap achieves efficiencies exceeding 95% in a single reaction, reducing the burden of steps, enzymes, and QC, and has been adopted by commercial products such as BioNTech/Pfizer (Source) ⚠️ — The trade-off between additional enzyme steps and cost versus slightly lower efficiency and template initiation sequence constraints has divided the industry into two paths. Second, the scale-up of the encapsulation mixer. Microfluidics provides the best reproducibility and property control with millisecond uniform mixing, but its low throughput (less than 100 mL/h) is a bottleneck at GMP scale (Source), and IJM is suitable for large-scale production, making it the choice for COVID commercial production, but its large minimum working volume makes it unsuitable for initial screening — meaning there is still no single technology that bridges discovery and clinical trials. Third, it is a regulatory classification. The EMA draft seeks to define nucleotides, cap reagents, and linear DNA templates as starting materials, and the entire composition, including lipids, as finished products (Source), but there is no international agreement on whether components (especially lipids) should be considered starting materials or excipients, so specifications and screening approaches vary by region (Source).Unresolved Questions: - Specific batch release specification values (lower limit of encapsulation efficiency %, dsRNA tolerance, residual DNA ng limit per dose, lower capping efficiency limit) are as per EMA/Ph.Eur. The original figures could not be confirmed (secondary sources only present items and definitions). - The specific design/judgment criteria and standardization status of the in-vitro efficacy (expression) test were confirmed only at an overview level. - The process details of the freeze-drying mRNA-LNP cycle (freezing rate, temperature-pressure of primary/secondary drying) are under the jurisdiction of adjacent node 4.2 and were not detailed in this section.

9.2 Viral vector & cell/gene therapy manufacturing

Place and role of this clause — the point of greatest inflection of the m

Ab ‘spine’

The standard flow of protein/monoclonal antibody (mAb) manufacturing that this report previously depicted — stable cell line culture → Protein A affinity capture → single large batch — is folded again from the root when it comes to viral vectors and cell and gene therapy (CGT). This section receives the starting material from node 1.3 (GMP plasmid, virus seed, HEK293 cell substrate), and in the case of autologous CAR-T, additionally receives leukapheresis collected from the patient, and processes the upstream process (USP: transfection-based vector production or T cell activation, transduction, and proliferation) and the downstream process (DSP: After going through clarification, affinity capture, ion exchange bin/full separation, and TFF), purified vector raw materials (in vivo gene therapy) or formulated and cryopreserved cell therapy finished products are handed over.

This entire verse will be readable if you first understand the two fundamental ‘inflections’. First, the viral vector can be the final ‘product’ itself (in vivo AAV gene therapy) or a ‘reagent’ to repair other cells (lenti/retroviral tools to insert genes into T cells in ex vivo CAR-T). Second, autologous cell therapy is not a mAb-type large single batch scale-UP, but the paradigm itself is overturned by scale-OUT, which operates multiple ‘1 patient = 1 batch’ in parallel. In reality, self-CGT is operated at ‘1 patient dose per manufacturing time’, and the manufacturing time is determined by the patient’s disease progression speed, not the production efficiency target, and usually takes 2 to 5 weeks (Source). As a result, economies of scale are not achieved, and instead cost of manufacturing (COGS), vein-to-vein time, and patient lot-to-patient consistency are the governing variables.

How It Works — From Upstream Production to Downstream Refining

AAV upstream (triple transfection).The standard production method for AAV vectors is ‘triple transfection’, which simultaneously introduces three types of plasmids into suspended (or attached) HEK293 cells: Rep/Cap containing the capsid serotype and replication mechanism, adenovirus helper functions (E2A/E4/VA RNA), and a vector plasmid carrying the transgene between the two ITRs, usually Co-transfect with PEI. The inherent limitation of this method is that ‘empty’ capsids with empty genomes are inevitably co-produced along with ‘full’ capsids containing the genome. Empty capsids are process-related impurities that are physically nearly identical to full capsids, making them extremely difficult to remove using standard chromatography (Source). As an alternative, stable producer cell lines are emerging, which integrate viral genes into the cell genome and then initiate production by induction (see ‘Trends’ below).Lenti/retro upstream. Lentiviruses are rendered replication-incompetent by transient transfection of a 4-plasmid (transfer·gag-pol·rev·VSV-G envelope) of a third-generation SIN (self-inactivating, 3’LTR deletion) design. It is common to set a harvest window of 36 to 48 hours for suspended HEK293 and increase the titer with a temperature shift (37 → 32 to 33℃) and sodium butyrate. Lenti is mostly consumed as a transduction reagent for ex vivo CAR-T, and lentiviral transduction provides high efficiency and stable and long-term expression (Source).AAV downstream (bin/pool separation is key). The downstream process begins with clarification (depth filtration) and cell lysis (breaking cells with detergents such as Triton The Camel single domain antibody-based CaptureSelect AAVX series affinity resin captures a wide range of serotypes, and in fact, Genethon reported that it purified AAV9 with CaptureSelect AAV9 resin with a recovery rate exceeding 80% on a 10L·50L scale (Source). The next critical step after affinity capture is bin/pool separation using anion exchange (AEX) — taking advantage of the difference that the pool capsid carrying the genome has a more negative charge. For example, a two-step ion exchange process that captures empty particles through cation exchange (Mustang S) and then captures grass particles through strong anion exchange (Mustang Q) can reduce empty particles to 0.8%, and ion exchange is virtually the only method that can actually separate empty and grass particles in large-scale actual processes (Source) ⚠️. Finally, it is concentrated, buffer exchanged, and formulated with TFF/UFDF, and finished with sterile filtration.Lenti/retro downstream. Lenti/retroviruses are unstable viruses with an envelope, so there is a large yield loss during the entire clarification, chromatography, and TFF process. TFF itself provides 90-100% recovery and 20-80-fold enrichment, but labile enveloped viruses can result in yield losses of up to 70% throughout downstream purification, and some vectors only achieve 5-30% recovery (Source).Autologous CAR-T workflow. The cell therapy flow is completely different from vector purification. The order is patient-derived leukocyte apheresis → T cell selection/concentration → activation (anti-CD3/CD28 beads, 2-3 days) → lenti/retro transduction (CAR gene insertion, transduction efficiency is usually less than 50%) → proliferation (more than 7 days) → washing, concentration, formulation → cryopreservation → bedside thawing and injection. A closed, semi-automated platform is used to reduce lot-to-lot variation during this process, and automated equipment such as CliniMACS Prodigy and Lonza Cocoon have been proven to reduce process variation across different T cell activation methods (Source).

Key parameters and materials — what to measure and what governs

The dominant indicator of AAV is capsid composition.One actual AAV starting material consisted of 57.4% full, 26.1% intermediate, and 16.5% empty, and after fractionation, the full capsid was concentrated to 91.1% purity (Source). Here, ‘intermediate’ capsids are not just harmless — they are just as infectious as full capsids, but they do not contribute to the efficacy of AAV products, and are a tricky component that skews purity (Source). The reason why empty capsids are a problem is because the product is administered based on vector genome (VG) titer: empty capsids are directly added to the total viral load during clinical administration, and the elevated viral load can worsen the capsid-induced immune response (Source). To tease out this subtle composition, AAV capsid characterization uses a combination of analytical ultracentrifugation (AUC), charge detection mass spectrometry (CDMS), NGS (PacBio), ddPCR, and CE-SDS (Source).Recoveries contrast sharply with mAbs. Downstream purification recoveries for AAV and lentiviral vectors are typically less than 50%, which contrasts sharply with the >90% recoveries routinely achieved in mAb platform processes (Source). This low recovery rate is a result of the vulnerability of the enveloped virus seen earlier (up to 70% loss) combined with the inevitable loss during the bin/pool separation process.The governing variables of CAR-T are the number of cells, time, and cost. Approximately 1.7 In centralized manufacturing, vein-to-vein time is 3 to 6 weeks, and next-day manufacturing produces functional CAR-Ts in 24 hours, but the actual vein-to-vein workflow still requires several days due to release testing (Source). The cost of this individualized manufacturing is also dominant: the manufacturing cost of autologous cell therapy is approximately $250,000 to $450,000 per injection due to individualized labor, dedicated equipment, and batch-specific QC overhead (Source) ⚠️; the price of FDA-approved CAR cell therapy is approximately $373,000 to $550,000 per injection; including hospitalization and ancillary treatments, the total cost is $1 million. It can exceed the dollar (Source).

Quality and regulation — two axes of safety: replication-competent viruses and insertional tumorigenesis

The core quality characteristics (CQA) of the vector include vector genome/capsid titer, full:empty ratio, identity (transgene sequence, repetitive region confirmed by NGS), efficacy (transgene mRNA/expressed protein in transduced cells), purity (empty capsid/HCP/residual plasmid/helper/benzonase), and sterility, endotoxin, and mycoplasma.

The most critical safety axis is the exclusion of replicable viruses — RCL for lenti, RCR for retro, and rcAAV (RCA) for AAV are tested on all lots before release. The FDA recommends that vector supernatants be tested sufficiently to ensure ‘95% detection probability when 1 RCR/dose equivalent is present’, that all ex vivo products be tested regardless of culture period, that 1% (maximum 10⁸) of end-of-production (EOP) cells be tested, and that bioassays be cultured for at least 5 passages (approximately 3 weeks) (Source).The second safety axis is insertional oncogenesis. Long-term follow-up of 15 years is recommended for individuals treated with integrating vectors, vector integration site analysis should be performed at 6, 12, 18, and 24 months, and investigation should be triggered if clonal integrants occur at a frequency exceeding 10-30% (Source).

There are also changes in potency management. FDA’s CGT efficacy assurance draft guidance (December 2023) goes beyond relying on a single potency test and defines the efficacy assurance strategy in five axes: process design, process control, raw material management, in-process testing, and potency lot release testing (Source). Related standards and guidelines include ICH Q5A(R2), FDA’s gene therapy IND CMC guidelines and ‘Manufacturing Changes and Comparability’ (July 2023), EU GMP Annex 1, Ph.Eur. 5.14, etc. However, one important gap identified in this section is that there is no harmonized quantitative regulatory limit for the full:empty ratio, so it is currently set individually as a standard for each product.

Differences by product type — opposite poles on one axis

Even within the same bioprocess, the nature of this section is diametrically different depending on the product type. mAb/recombinant protein scales up a single large batch with stable cell culture + Protein A, and is the polar opposite without the concept of empty/full. AAV (in vivo gene therapy) is a vector itself that is a raw drug, and is characterized by triple transfection, blank/pool isolation, and rcAAV testing. Lenti/Retro is mainly consumed as a transduction reagent for ex vivo CAR-T, and RCL/RCR testing and SIN design are key. Self-CGT is scale-OUT, dominated by patient-derived starting materials (apheresis), vein-to-vein, and ultra-expensive COGS, and economies of scale are not established. On the other hand, allogeneic CGT enables off-the-shelf products that can be used on multiple patients, lowering individual manufacturing time and costs and allowing standardized quality control (Source) ⚠️, but challenges remain such as immune rejection and persistence. There are also clear trade-offs depending on the transduction method: whereas lenti provides stable and long-term expression, mRNA provides only temporary expression, but there is little risk of insertion mutation, so safety and sustainability are at odds (Source). In short, the critical difference between mRNA-LNP/classical vaccines and CGT is that in CGT, ‘living cells’ and ‘replicable virus risk’ are the central axes of safety and quality.

Practice status and recent trends

The current standard is transient triple/four-plasmid transfection + affinity capture + ion exchange bin/full separation + TFF, and the mainstream of autologous CAR-T is centralized closed/semi-automated manufacturing. The limitations are the same as previously seen - low downstream recovery (less than 50%) (Source), burden of empty capsids, plasmid supply/cost, batch variation, long vein-to-vein, very expensive COGS, and challenges in potency testing.

The flow of change over the past three years can be divided into six categories. (1) Move to stable AAV/LV producer cell lines — Asimov reported titers up to 6E15 vg/L before purification with stable AAV producer cell lines in October 2025, and claims that stable clones eliminate the need for expensive GMP plasmids, simplify scale-up, and minimize batch-to-batch variation, but most programs still rely on batch production to transfect multiple plasmids each batch. Depends (Source) ⚠️. (2) Spread of suspended, intensified, and continuous/fixed-bed lenti production. (3) Attempts at decentralized/point-of-care manufacturing and rapid CAR-T within 24 hours to several days. (4) Shift of attention to homogeneous off-the-shelf CARs (Source) ⚠️. (5) Attempts to replace transduction itself with non-viral gene delivery such as transposon·CRISPR knock-in·mRNA. (6) Evolution of the regulatory framework, including the FDA draft efficacy assurance (December 2023) and CGT CMC flexibility (Source).Issues:There are four tensions in this section that have not yet been settled. First, is the future standard for vector production transient transfection or stable producer cell lines? — Transient method is the overwhelming current standard that is advantageous for early clinical trials as it can flexibly change the envelope, accessory genes, and ratios, while stable producer lines (Asimov AAV Edge, ELEVECTA) emphasize GMP plasmid removal, batch consistency, and scale-up. However, it is too early to view stable stocks as a mature fact as their regulatory history and commercial scale performance are still shallow and they are strongly vendor-led. Second, the dominant model among autologous vs. allogeneic — allogeneic is superior in manufacturing economics, and autologous is superior in biological sustainability and safety, so a single winner has not yet been determined. Third, Gap between regulatory expectations and practical capabilities for empty/empty control — High-resolution analysis (AUC is the gold standard) captures even minute compositions, but virtually the only means of separation on a large scale is serotype-dependent ion exchange, and there is no harmonized quantitative regulatory limit for full:empty, so it is temporarily operated as a product-specific standard. Fourth, RCL test method — The FDA recommendation is a minimum of 5 passages (about 3 weeks) and a completely cell-based assay to catch slow-growing viruses, but fresh infusion products cannot wait that period, so rapid assays such as VSV-G qPCR are used as a practical alternative. The expiration date of the product forces the selection of a testing method.Unresolved Questions: ① The harmonized quantitative regulatory limit of the full:empty ratio (allowable empty % upper limit for each approved product) only confirmed the absence of a standard and did not confirm specific numerical standards. ② The specific protocol of the AAV rcAAV (RCA) test (infectious cell passage assay details, tolerance limits) is not as detailed as the lenti RCL and only covers the frame level. ③ The detailed unit process of allogeneic CGT manufacturing (HLA editing, multiple gene knock-out, expanded scale) and quantitative comparison with self-comparison are only at an overview level. ④ Industry benchmark actual measurements of commercial scale AAV titer (vg/L) and lenti functional titer (TU/mL) by serotype are only approximated by vendor claims (6E15 vg/L) and research protocol levels.

9.3 Vaccine-specific operations

Role — Set of points at which the m

Ab spine collapses

The process spine that this report has followed so far (cell culture → capture chromatography → purification) assumes monoclonal antibodies (m

Ab) and recombinant proteins. However, vaccines are heterogeneous in terms of what the “product” is. It may be a whole inactivated virus, a split subunit antigen from a split virus, a conjugate of a bacterial polysaccharide attached to a protein, a recombinant protein or nanoparticle, and an adjuvant is added to it. This section is a collection of points where the m

Ab spine is disrupted, replaced, and reversed, and deals with antigen production and adjuvant mixing for classical, protein, and polysaccharide conjugate vaccines, excluding mRNA-LNP (9.1) and viral vector/CGT (9.2), among the architectures for each product type in Part 9. Influenza vaccines are representative examples of antigen production (egg/cell/recombinant) and inactivation/cleavage, bacterial polysaccharide vaccines are representative examples of glycoconjugation, and adjuvants traverse these various modalities. The antigen source (egg/cell/recombinant determination, cell substrate selection) is transferred from nodes 1.1 and 1.3, and the purified antigen solution, conjugate solution, and adjuvant bulk from here are then transferred to formulation/filling (4.x) and QC (6.x).

How it works — four blocks

The process is largely divided into four blocks. (A) Antigen production, (B) Inactivation/cleavage, (C) Glycoconjugation, (D) Adjuvant formulation.

(A) Antigen manufacturing — Influenza is the prototype.There are three paths to obtaining viral antigens, and the influenza vaccine is a representative example of commercialization of all three platforms. The first is egg-based, in which seed viruses are inoculated into the allantois of embryonated eggs cultured for 9 to 12 days, grown for 2 to 3 days at 33 to 35°C, and then allantoic fluid is recovered. Typically, 8 to 10 mL of allantoic fluid is obtained per embryonic egg (Source). ⚠️ The recovered and concentrated virus is purified by zonal ultracentrifugation using a sucrose density gradient (20-50%) to collect the virus band (Source). ⚠️ A chronic weakness in the embryonic egg process is the so-called egg-adaptation. In particular, the cause of the reduced vaccine effectiveness for the H3N2 component is that the receptor binding site and domain specificity are modified as the virus passes through eggs and adapts to the avian receptor (Source).

The second is cell-based, where mammalian cells such as MDCK and Vero are cultured in a bioreactor/microcarrier to multiply the virus. MDCK cells are considered suitable for manufacturing influenza vaccines because they can avoid undesirable egg-adapted antigenic mutations that occur during passage of embryonic eggs (Source). The only cell-based inactivated influenza vaccine licensed in the United States is Seqirus’ Flucelvax Quadrivalent, which is manufactured with MDCK cells in serum-free suspension and received FDA approval in 2016 (Source).

The third is recombinant, which produces HA directly by expressing baculovirus/Sf9 in insect cells (e.g. Flublok, RIV). This method eliminates egg-adaptation because there is no seed virus itself, and the recombinant influenza vaccine (RIV) contains 45 µg HA, three times the standard dose (15 µg HA per strain) (Source). Additionally, because egg-adapted seeds are not used, the recombinant HA antigen contained in the vaccine is believed to be completely identical to the HA of the vaccine reference virus (Source).(B) Inactivation & Cleavage — Eliminates infectivity and reduces reactogenicity.Inactivated virus vaccines eliminate infectivity with alkylating agents. The chemistry of the two representative reagents is different: formaldehyde (FA) cross-links between molecular structures, and β-propiolactone (βPL) acylates and alkylates molecules (Source). Examples of experimental conditions include 0.02% formalin (2-7°C, 24 hours) and 0.1% βPL (Source). The two reagents also have different buffering requirements. βPL inactivation requires a higher buffering capacity (e.g., 125 mM citric acid, pH 7.8) to prevent the pH from dropping significantly during the reaction, whereas formaldehyde is performed in phosphate buffer (Source). The reaction termination and removal methods are also contrasted. βPL activity is stopped by autohydrolysis when heated at 37°C for 2 hours, and formaldehyde is removed by diafiltration using a 100 kDa centrifugal filter (Source).

The inactivated whole virion is again “split” by the surfactant. Surfactants such as Triton If HA/NA is further purified, it becomes a subunit vaccine. Removal of the splitting agent varies depending on the method. Triton X-100 is a hydrophobic adsorption resin (Amberlite(C) Glycoconjugation — The chemistry that converts a polysaccharide into a T cell-dependent antigen.Bacterial capsular polysaccharide is itself a T cell-independent antigen, so it induces only a brief immune response and leaves no memory in infants and young children. Therefore, soluble polysaccharides are usually covalently bound to a carrier protein to stimulate T cell-dependent mechanisms to strengthen antigen-specific immune responses (Source). CRM197 (non-toxic diphtheria variant), tetanus toxoid (TT), diphtheria toxoid (DT), and protein D are used as carriers. The activation chemistry is bifurcated, and this choice determines the fate of the sugar ring. Reductive amination oxidizes the polysaccharide with sodium periodate to create an aldehyde, which is then reductively combined with a carrier amine, and at this time, the sugar ring is opened (ring opening). CDAP cyanylation activates the hydroxyl group of the polysaccharide into cyanate ester to form an isourea bond with the carrier amine, and the hexose ring is intact even after cyanylation (Source).

The process sequence is as follows. Sizing (size reduction) of the capsular polysaccharide to the target molecular weight → chemical activation → buffer exchange through ultrafiltration (UF) → combined with purified CRM197 → purification with UF → finally filtered through a 0.22 µm filter (Source). ⚠️(This process sequence description is based on evidence with medium confidence.) Multivalent conjugate vaccines may use different carriers for each serogroup. In the example of the meningococcal pentavalent conjugate vaccine, serogroup A·X polysaccharide is bound to tetanus toxoid (TT), and serogroup C·W·Y polysaccharide is bound to recombinant CRM197 (Source).

(D) Adjuvant formulations — Immunity-boosting formulations.Adjuvant formulations come in many classes with different compositions and physical forms. The oldest aluminum salt adsorbs antigens to surfaces. At neutral pH, aluminum hydroxide has a positive charge and aluminum phosphate has a negative charge. Adsorption of antigens to aluminum adjuvant promotes phagocytosis and slows the spread of antigens at the injection site, strengthening the initial immune response (Source). However, aluminum salts only selectively stimulate Th2 immune responses and do not induce cytotoxic T cell responses or cell-mediated immunity (Source).

The oil-in-water emulsion series is next. MF59 is an oil-in-water emulsion of metabolizable squalene (4.3%), stabilized with Tween 80 (0.5%) and Span 85 (0.5%), has a droplet size of approximately 160 nm, and is used in influenza vaccines such as Fluad (Source). AS03 is an oil-in-water emulsion composed of α-tocopherol, squalene, and polysorbate 80. It is characterized by α-tocopherol having its own immunomodulatory effect, and has been used in pandemic influenza vaccines such as Pandemrix (Source).

There are also adjuvant systems that combine TLR agonists. AS04 is a system in which MPL, a TLR4 agonist, is adsorbed onto aluminum hydroxide/phosphate and is used for Fendrix (hepatitis B) and Cervarix (HPV) (Source). AS01 is a system containing two immunostimulants, MPL and QS-21, in DOPC/cholesterol liposomes, and cholesterol plays a role in suppressing the hemolytic activity of QS-21. AS01B contains 50 µg of MPL and 50 µg of QS-21 per dose and is used in Shingrix, Mosquirix, and Arexvy (Source).

Key parameters and materials

The materials and specifications that penetrate the above blocks are summarized as follows. In terms of antigen production, embryonic eggs (9-12 days old, grown at 33-35°C, allantoic fluid approx. 8-10 mL/egg), sucrose 20-50% zone ultracentrifugation (Source) ⚠️, serum-free floating MDCK·Vero cell substrate (Source), The baculovirus/Sf9 expression system is the key. In inactivation/splitting, formalin (e.g. 0.02%, phosphate buffer, 2-7°C for 24 h) and βPL (e.g. 0.1%, 125 mM citric acid pH 7.8, stopped at 37°C for 2 h) (Source), Triton X-100·sodium as a splitting agent. deoxycholate (Source) and Amberlite XAD resin for removal appear. In conjugation, the list of ingredients includes a carrier (CRM197·TT·DT·protein D), an activator (sodium periodate, CDAP) (Source), UF buffer exchange and 0.22 µm final filtration (Source) ⚠️. Adjuvant materials include squalene (MF59 approximately 4.3%), Tween 80 (0.5%), Span 85 (0.5%) ([Source] (https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC12180328/)), α-tocopherol (AS03), MPL·QS-21·DOPC/cholesterol liposome (AS01B = MPL 50 µg + QS-21) 50 µg)(Source). Typical quantitative indicators of input and output include the influenza standard dose of 15 µg HA/week (RIV is 45 µg) ([Source] (https://academic.oup.com/cid/article/73/11/1973/6318730)), adjuvant droplet size of approximately 160 nm, and the free polysaccharide content of the conjugate vaccine unit price bulk.

Quality and Regulation

A characteristic of vaccine QC is that the definition of “potency” and testing methods are fundamentally different for each product modality.The compendial titer test for influenza is single radioimmunodiffusion (SRID), which has been used for over 40 years. Polyclonal antiserum is immobilized on an agarose gel, HA is diffused, and the HA content is quantified by the diameter of the sediment ring (Source). The problem is that this only internationally recognized test is a bottleneck in vaccine shipments. SRID is labor-intensive, relatively low-sensitivity, and difficult to automate, making it time-consuming. In particular, the time it takes to create strain-specific sheep antisera and calibration antigen standards delays vaccine shipments (Source).

The CQA of the conjugate vaccine is completely different. Key management items include free saccharide content, sugar:protein ratio (binding index), molecular size distribution, and O-acetylation level. In the actual measurement example of the meningococcal conjugate vaccine, free polysaccharide was measured up to 15% in MenA·C·Y·W and up to 20% in MenX based on the unit price bulk conjugate (Source). There is one particularly big paradigm shift. In 1998, WHO revised the production and quality control recommendations for Hib conjugate vaccines on the grounds that biological (animal) potency tests had a low correlation with clinical efficacy in infants and children, and replaced potency tests for batch shipment with physical and chemical tests from animal tests (Source). This is the turning point where conjugate vaccine QC moves from biological potency to physicochemical properties.

The governing standards are organized by product into the WHO TRS Annex (Hib TRS 897, Meningococcus TRS 962, etc.), Ph.Eur. (Split Virion/Subunit Influenza Vaccine Monograph), USP, NIBSC (International Standard/SRID Reference Reagent), FDA CBER, and EMA. On the adjuvant side, the fact that the ingredient alone has no adjuvant effect and only works as a combination — represented by AS03 and AS01 — is the key from a regulatory and quality perspective, and management targets include droplet size distribution, squalene, α-tocopherol, and polysorbate content, MPL and QS-21 content, and sterility and endotoxin.

Differences by product type

This section itself contains the diversity of vaccine modalities. Inactivation (whole/split/subunit)The vaccine follows the overall flow of antigen manufacturing → inactivation → (splitting) as seen previously. In Live herbal intoxication (LAIV), inactivation and division disappear, and instead, reassortment and securing low-temperature-adapted seeds become the key (however, this detail is an adjacent area within the scope of this section and is only covered in overview, and quantitative verification is insufficient — [uncertain]). In recombinant protein/subunit/VLP/nanoparticle, antigen production is replaced by expression (BEVS Sf9, CHO, etc.), inactivation and splitting are unnecessary, and purified antigen is instead self-assembled into nanoparticles. An example is the Novavax method, which infects Sf9 moth cells with a baculovirus containing a modified spike gene, expresses and harvests the spike protein on the cell membrane, and then assembles it into synthetic lipid nanoparticles of about 50 nm ([Source] (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novavax_COVID-19_vaccine)). ⚠️(medium evidence) This is a typical example of using insect cell expression instead of mAb-type cell culture/capture chromatography. Toxoid (diphtheria, tetanus) is toxoidized by fermentation of toxin followed by formaldehyde inactivation, and polysaccharide-conjugated vaccine is a chemical-centered process that obtains capsular polysaccharide through bacterial fermentation and performs glycoconjugation, which is completely different from the viral antigen flow.

The identity of this clause becomes clearer when compared to the adjacent product modality. There is no such manipulation in mAb. In mRNA-LNP (9.1), antigen production, inactivation, cleavage, and conjugation are all disrupted because the antigen is translated in the body, and LNP itself has a self-adjuvant nature, so external adjuvants are usually not used. In viral vectors (9.2), inactivation is contraindicated because the vector itself is the product. On the other hand, adjuvants are commonly applied across protein, inactivated, and polysaccharide vaccines.

Practices and changes

The current standard is still embryonic egg-based split/subunit influenza vaccines, which are the world’s mainstays, but cell-based (Flucelvax, MDCK, 2016 FDA) (Source) and recombinant (Flublok/RIV) (Source) are gaining ground with the advantages of egg-adaptation avoidance and pandemic scalability. Combination vaccines are evolving to become more expensive (pneumococcal PCV13 → PCV15/20/21). There are roughly five axes of change in recent years. (1) Research on titer methods to replace SRID is accelerating, and mAb-based ELISA, BLI, and structure-selective biophysical analysis aim to alleviate the bottleneck of reference reagents for each strain (Source). (2) Antigen-sparing using adjuvants has emerged as a key strategy for pandemic preparedness. This is because adjuvants allow the amount of antigen per dose to be reduced without sacrificing efficacy in situations of outbreaks or supply shortages (Source). ⚠️(based on blog·medium) (3) The new adjuvant franchise has expanded (GSK AS01 → Shingrix·Arexvy·Mosquirix, Novavax Matrix-M, Dynavax CpG1018). (4) As conjugate vaccine titers are converted to physical and chemical tests, animal testing is being reduced (Source). (5) New platforms, such as mRNA influenza, are beginning to bypass classical vaccine manipulation itself.

Limitations and unresolved points are also clear. Vulnerability of egg supply during SRID bottlenecks and pandemics, supply and standardization of QS-21, a saponin derived from plant (Quillaja saponaria), lot-to-lot binding homogeneity and free polysaccharide management of conjugate vaccines, recombinant expression and stability of difficult antigens, and lack of complete elucidation of the adjuvant mechanism of action, etc. remain.

Major players include Seqirus/CSL (Flucelvax, Fluad=MF59), Sanofi (Flublok, Fluzone), and GSK (Fluarix/FluLaval) in influenza, and adjuvants. GSK (AS01, AS03, AS04), Novavax (Matrix-M), Dynavax (CpG1018), Croda/Brenntag (Alhydrogel), Pfizer (Prevnar 20), Merck (Vaxneuvance PCV15, Capvaxive PCV21), Serum Institute of India (Meningococcal NmCV-5), etc. in conjugate vaccines, and carriers. CRM197 is provided by suppliers such as Fina Biosolutions.

Issue

There are three points in this section where the fodder is ground.

Are cell/recombinant influenza vaccines clinically more effective than embryonic egg vaccines?On the one hand, there is real-world evidence that cell-based (MDCK)/recombinant vaccines are superior in antigen matching by avoiding egg-adaptation, and are more effective in reducing influenza-like diseases and hospitalizations, especially in seasons when H3N2 is a problem. On the other hand, some randomized controlled immunogenicity trials report that the differences between the three platforms are not significant or are season dependent. Because dominance occurs primarily in years where there is a large discrepancy between circulating strains and vaccine strains, differences in endpoints between observational studies (effectiveness) and RCTs (immunogenicity) create gaps in interpretation.Which is superior between reductive amination and CDAP cyanylation as a conjugate vaccine activation chemistry? It has been reported that cyanylation (CDAP) preserves the sugar ring and induces higher opsonophagotic antibody and 19A cross-reactivity in pneumococcal 19F than reductive amination, while reductive amination has been widely verified and used in major commercial conjugate vaccines such as Prevnar, and has a strong robustness and regulatory history. The optimal chemistry is different for each serotype and polysaccharide structure, and the effect of ring opening on the creation of new epitopes is serotype-specific, making generalization difficult.Will SRID be maintained or replaced in influenza titer testing? The regulatory side is trying to maintain SRID as the only internationally recognized test that has been verified for 40 years (changing the method is a large verification burden), and the industry is pressing for the introduction of an alternative method due to delays in shipment due to bottlenecks, low sensitivity, and inability to automate reference reagents for each strain. It is a trade-off between the need for speed and automation and regulatory continuity and intercomparability of standard products, and the alternative law has not yet fully proven its correlation and versatility with SRID.

Unresolved Questions

  • The quantitative range of the adjuvant lot shipment specifications (upper droplet size limit, MPL/QS-21 content specification, squalene/α-tocopherol content allowable range) could not be confirmed as a numerical specification due to limited access to individual manufacturer/pharmacopoeial specifications.
  • The details of the rearrangement/cold-adapted seeds of herbal medicine intoxication (LAIV) and the toxoidization (formaldehyde) process are adjacent to the scope of this section and are only covered in outline (quantitative verification is insufficient).
  • Quantitative evidence on glycoconjugation carrier overload (carrier-induced epitopic suppression) and carrier selection trade-offs in multivalent conjugate vaccines remains at an overview level.
